        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.7b12155"><meta property="og:title" content="Few-Layer MXenes Delaminated via High-Energy Mechanical Milling for Enhanced Sodium-Ion Batteries Performance"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/acsami.7b12155.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="The global availability of sodium makes the exploration of superior sodium-ion batteries attractive for energy storage application. MXenes, as one of the most promising anodes for sodium-ion batteries, have been reported to have many advantages, such as high electronic conductivity and a hydrophilic surface. However, the compact multilayer structure and deficient delamination significantly inhibits their application, requiring high energy and showing decreased storage capacity and poor rate capabilities. Few-layer MXene has been proved to benefit superior electrochemical properties with a better ionic conductivity and two-dimensional layer structure. Herein, we report scale delamination of few-layer MXene nanosheets as anodes for sodium-ion batteries, which are prepared via an organic solvent assist high-energy mechanical-milling method. This approach efficiently prevents the oxidation of MXene and produces few-layer nanosheets structure, facilitating fast electron transport and Na+ diffusion. Electrochemical tests demonstrate that the few-layer MXenes show high specific capacity, excellent cycle stability, and good rate performance. Specifically, few-layer MXene nanosheets deliver a high reversible capacity of 267 mA h g–1 at a current density of 0.1 A g–1. After cycling 1500 cycles at a high rate of 1 A g–1, a reversible capacity of 76 mA h g–1 could be maintained."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/acsami.7b12155.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90f6e97f8e2a775c-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e97f8e2a775c-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: 'e4f8f1f3-ba33-4c02-a0b8-ab115b612242'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e97f8e2a775c-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Few-Layer MXenes Delaminated via High-Energy Mechanical Milling for Enhanced Sodium-Ion Batteries Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b12155", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Few-Layer MXenes Delaminated via High-Energy Mechanical Milling for Enhanced Sodium-Ion Batteries Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b12155", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Few-Layer MXenes Delaminated via High-Energy Mechanical Milling for Enhanced Sodium-Ion Batteries Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b12155", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Few-Layer MXenes Delaminated via High-Energy Mechanical Milling for Enhanced Sodium-Ion Batteries Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b12155", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Few-Layer MXenes Delaminated via High-Energy Mechanical Milling for Enhanced Sodium-Ion Batteries Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b12155", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Few-Layer MXenes Delaminated via High-Energy Mechanical Milling for Enhanced Sodium-Ion Batteries Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b12155", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Few-Layer MXenes Delaminated via High-Energy Mechanical Milling for Enhanced Sodium-Ion Batteries Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b12155", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Few-Layer MXenes Delaminated via High-Energy Mechanical Milling for Enhanced Sodium-Ion Batteries Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b12155", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Few-Layer MXenes Delaminated via High-Energy Mechanical Milling for Enhanced Sodium-Ion Batteries Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b12155", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

aria-expanded="false"><i class="icon-angle-down"></i><i class="icon-angle-up"></i></a><div data-db-target-of="article_header-history" class="dropBlock__holder" aria-hidden="true"><div class="articleHeaderHistoryDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderHistoryDropzone"><div class="article__history"> <h3 class="article__history__header">Publication History</h3><ul class="hidden" property="articleSection">research-article</div><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2017 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_rightPermissionsLink"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone4" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone4"><div class="articleRightsPermissionsLink"><a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D39610%26pageCount%3D8%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DYuting%2BWu%252C%2BPing%2BNie%252C%2BJiang%2BWang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D9%26issueNum%3D45%26contentID%3Dacsami.7b12155%26title%3DFew-Layer%2BMXenes%2BDelaminated%2Bvia%2BHigh-Energy%2BMechanical%2BMilling%2Bfor%2BEnhanced%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%2BPerformance%26numPages%3D8%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D39617%26publicationDate%3DNovember%2B2017" data-id="article_rights_permissions">Request reuse permissions</a></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_header-metrics-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="article_header-metrics-dropzone"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="f_tgr1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/medium/am-2017-121554_0006.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/large/am-2017-121554_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b12155&amp;id=f_tgr1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">The global availability of sodium makes the exploration of superior sodium-ion batteries attractive for energy storage application. MXenes, as one of the most promising anodes for sodium-ion batteries, have been reported to have many advantages, such as high electronic conductivity and a hydrophilic surface. However, the compact multilayer structure and deficient delamination significantly inhibits their application, requiring high energy and showing decreased storage capacity and poor rate capabilities. Few-layer MXene has been proved to benefit superior electrochemical properties with a better ionic conductivity and two-dimensional layer structure. Herein, we report scale delamination of few-layer MXene nanosheets as anodes for sodium-ion batteries, which are prepared via an organic solvent assist high-energy mechanical-milling method. This approach efficiently prevents the oxidation of MXene and produces few-layer nanosheets structure, facilitating fast electron transport and Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion. Electrochemical tests demonstrate that the few-layer MXenes show high specific capacity, excellent cycle stability, and good rate performance. Specifically, few-layer MXene nanosheets deliver a high reversible capacity of 267 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at a current density of 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. After cycling 1500 cycles at a high rate of 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, a reversible capacity of 76 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> could be maintained.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D39610%26pageCount%3D8%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DYuting%2BWu%252C%2BPing%2BNie%252C%2BJiang%2BWang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D9%26issueNum%3D45%26contentID%3Dacsami.7b12155%26title%3DFew-Layer%2BMXenes%2BDelaminated%2Bvia%2BHigh-Energy%2BMechanical%2BMilling%2Bfor%2BEnhanced%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%2BPerformance%26numPages%3D8%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D39617%26publicationDate%3DNovember%2B2017" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2017 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291517&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Batteries" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Batteries" class="article__tags__link">Batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291688&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Layered materials" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Layered%20materials" class="article__tags__link">Layered materials</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292017&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Solvents" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Solvents" class="article__tags__link">Solvents</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292522&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Two dimensional materials" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Two%20dimensional%20materials" class="article__tags__link">Two dimensional materials</a></li></ul></div></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Mxene&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_MXene">MXene</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Few+Layers&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_few%20layers">few layers</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=High-energy+Mechanical+Milling&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_high-energy%20mechanical%20milling">high-energy mechanical milling</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=DMSO&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_DMSO">DMSO</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Anode&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_anode">anode</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20batteries">sodium-ion batteries</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i1">Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">Electrochemical energy storage is key to modulate variable renewable resources for large-scale application, which can efficiently store and release electricity. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4" aria-label="reference 1 to 4">(1-4)</a> Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with advantages of low cost and high stability have been regarded as one of the most promising battery systems for energy storage. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5 ref6'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref6" aria-label="reference 5 and 6">(5, 6)</a> Because of the similar physical and chemical properties between sodium and lithium, electrode materials for SIBs are basically selected from those for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs). Compared with LIBs, the greatest challenge of SIBs is sluggish reaction kinetics due to the larger ionic size of Na ions (1.02 Å) and atomic mass. Various cathodes have been intensively reported for SIBs, such as tunnel-type transition-metal oxide, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7 ref8'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7 ref8" aria-label="reference 7 and 8">(7, 8)</a> Prussian blue analogues, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9" aria-label="reference 9">(9)</a> and organic cathodes. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10" aria-label="reference 10">(10)</a> However, the most conventional graphite-based anode materials provide limited interlayer space for sodium-ions intercalation. Thus, there is a strong requirement to investigate eligible anode materials for sodium-ion batteries. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11" aria-label="reference 11">(11)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">MXenes are a new family of two-dimensional transition-metal carbides/carbonitrides with a general chemical formula of M<sub><i>n</i>+1</sub>X<sub><i>n</i></sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15" aria-label="reference 12 to 15">(12-15)</a> MXenes are derived from MAX phases by selectively etching out the A atom layers, where M is a transition metal, A is an element from groups IIIA or IVA, and X is C and/or N. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16 ref17'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16 ref17" aria-label="reference 16 and 17">(16, 17)</a> The first achieved and most studied multilayer MXene is Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> obtained by treating Ti<sub>3</sub>AlC<sub>2</sub> with hydrofluoric acid (HF) or a mixture of lithium fluoride and hydrochloric acid. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18 ref19'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref19" aria-label="reference 18 and 19">(18, 19)</a> The etching process induces the presence of chemical functional groups T<sub><i>x</i></sub> on surfaces including hydroxyl, oxygen, or fluorine groups. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a> MXenes with desirable advantages of fast charge-transfer kinetics, strong interfacial coupling, and large active surface area have been integrated in many applications such as catalysis, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19 ref21'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19 ref21" aria-label="reference 19 and 21">(19, 21)</a> electronic devices, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22" aria-label="reference 22">(22)</a> energy storage. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23 ref24 ref25'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref24 ref25" aria-label="reference 23 to 25">(23-25)</a> In particular, MXene is an emerging electrode material for SIBs. For example, Ti<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> and V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27" aria-label="reference 27">(27)</a> exhibit outstanding superior electrochemical performance, especially rate capability for batteries application due to the metallic conductivity (2.4 × 10<sup>5</sup> S m<sup>–1</sup>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26 ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26 ref28" aria-label="reference 26 and 28">(26, 28)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">The single-/few-layer MXenes not only provide the benefit of full utilization of surface and electrolyte access but also provide a higher negative potential facilitating their composition with other materials <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29" aria-label="reference 29">(29)</a> or polymers <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30 ref31'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30 ref31" aria-label="reference 30 and 31">(30, 31)</a> to form hierarchical composite. The multilayer structure of MXene can be delaminated by the intercalation of water or organic molecules, such as dimethyl sulfoxide (DMSO), urea, and isopropyl amine, followed by sonication. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32 ref33'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref33" aria-label="reference 32 and 33">(32, 33)</a>However, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> is known to spontaneously transform into more stable metal oxides by reacting with dissolved oxygen and water. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34 ref35'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34 ref35" aria-label="reference 34 and 35">(34, 35)</a> This common and inevitable phenomenon is involved in most delamination processes. The oxidation of MXenes causes the reduction of electrical conductivity and the passivation of the reactive interface. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36" aria-label="reference 36">(36)</a> In addition, the undesirable F functional groups show little reduction during current delamination methods, which has been a great challenge since the first report in 2011. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" aria-label="reference 37">(37)</a> Moreover, a relatively low yield of delaminated MXenes also limits their application. Recently, Naguibet al. reported an organic-based-driven delamination of titanium carbide for aluminum-oxoanion-functionalized monolayer or bilayer MXene with a 1.05 g L<sup>–1</sup> yield. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref38" aria-label="reference 38">(38)</a> Nevertheless, the delaminated MXenes are obtained still by dispersion in H<sub>2</sub>O followed by the sonication procedure, which do not restrain the oxidation process.</div><div class="NLM_p last">Herein we reported a novel method to prepare few-layer Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>X</i></sub> with high yield and great stability by high-energy mechanical milling method (HEMM) in organic solvents. With the assistance of dimethyl sulfoxide (DMSO), multilayer Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>X</i></sub> was delaminated into few-layer structure without oxidation under the high temperature and pressure induced by HEMM. Importantly, the as-fabricated few-layer Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>X</i></sub> possessed a large specific surface area, good access to electrolyte, and short diffusion paths for both ion and electron, thus exhibiting excellent performance for SIBs including high capacities, impressive rate capabilities, and long cycling stabilities. This unique approach combining liquid delamination with mechanical delamination is an effective and simple technique for large-scale production of few-layer MXenes.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">High-energy mechanical milling is considered as one of the major techniques for synthesizing nanomaterials. HEMM technique not only can be applied for mass production but also provide enough energy for chemical reactions. It was previously reported that amorphous red phosphorus was transformed into orthorhombic black phosphorus due to the high temperature and pressure when using HEMM technique. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref39" aria-label="reference 39">(39)</a> Dispersion of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> in organic solvents could effectively prevent their oxidation. Among various organic guests, DMSO is one of the most successful intercalators. In addition, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> can form the stable dispersion in DMSO with long-term duration. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40" aria-label="reference 40">(40)</a> Herein, DMSO was chosen to be an ideal organic solvent for HEMM treatment.</div><div class="NLM_p">As schematically illustrated in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>, we fabricated few-layered Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> with DMSO via HEMM technique as ascribed f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO. Simply, 1 g of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> MXene powder was poured into the HEMM vessel immersed into 30 mL of DMSO solvent and the few-layered MXene could be collected in large scale after a certain milling time treatment. To identify the function of DMSO solvent, the MXene milled without DMSO was prepared under the same conditions, labeled as Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled. The structure and phase characteristics of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled, and f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO samples are determined by X-ray diffraction (XRD) as shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>a. The XRD pattern of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO is similar to that of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF. The (002) peak of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> is broadened and shifted to a lower 2θ value after HEMM treatment in DMSO, indicating a larger interlayer distance for f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO sample (from 9.6 to 12.6 Å). The XRD pattern of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> after HEMM treatment without solvent clearly shows the conversion from MXene to anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> with some partly graphitic carbon, which can be confirmed by the appearance of peaks at 25.28° and 48.05°. As an effective stabilizer, DMSO reduces the probability of MXene’s oxidation process with the trace amount of oxygen and water under HEMM treatment. To identify the influence of different solvents on the <i>d</i>-spacing of the MXene, f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMF, and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_EtOH samples are analyzed by XRD measurement (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/suppl_file/am7b12155_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a> of the Supporting Information). The samples treated with different solvents all exhibited a similar (002) peak shift with corresponding interlayer distance of about 12.6, 10.54, and 10.81 Å, respectively. These results clearly indicated that the interlayer spacing of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> all increases after HEMM treatment in different solvents. The interlayer spacing of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> in DMSO treatment is larger than other milled samples, suggesting its high effectiveness for delamination. The higher boiling point of DMSO (189 °C) compared with that of DMF (153 °C) and EtOH (78 °C) possibly benefits the reversible intercalation process, resulting in a larger interlayer space. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32" aria-label="reference 32">(32)</a> The Raman spectra of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled are presented in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>b. The f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO sample exhibits three broad Raman peaks locating at around 250, 410, and 710 cm<sup>–1</sup>, attributed to the vibrations from nonstoichiometric titanium carbide. Raman spectra confirmed the appearance of carbon layer in Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled sample with two broad peaks ranging from 1000 and 1600 cm<sup>–1</sup> characteristic for the D- and G-modes of carbon. The Raman spectrum of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled also showed a strong peak at 144 cm<sup>–1</sup> together with three other peaks at 394, 513, and 635 cm<sup>–1</sup>, assigned to the anatase vibrational. The presence of carbon sheets and TiO<sub>2</sub> particles on the surface implies that Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled has reacted with oxygen. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41" aria-label="reference 41">(41)</a></div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/medium/am-2017-121554_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/large/am-2017-121554_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. Schematic illustration of scale delamination of few-layer Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>nanosheets by HEMM with DMSO solvent.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/large/am-2017-121554_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b12155&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/medium/am-2017-121554_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/large/am-2017-121554_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. (a, b) XRD patterns and Raman spectra of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled, and f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO samples; (c) SEM image of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF; (d–f) SEM and TEM images of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO (inset in part (f) is SAED).</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/large/am-2017-121554_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b12155&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">SEM image of stacked Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF is presented in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>c, indicating that HF treatment results in the successful removal of the Al layers from MAX phase. The energy-dispersive spectrometer (EDS) pattern of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF further confirms the successful exfoliation and the presence of F and O, indicating possible surface termination (like F, O, and OH groups) in the surface of MXene (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/suppl_file/am7b12155_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>). SEM and TEM images of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO clearly showed thin and transparent nanoflakes (in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>d,e), demonstrating the successful delamination of MXene. The average diameter of the nanoflakes is around 500 nm, which is obviously smaller than Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/suppl_file/am7b12155_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>). TEM images of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled, and samples milled in different organic solvents are shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/suppl_file/am7b12155_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a>. The stacked multilayer structures were found in Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMF, and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_EtOH samples. However, TEM images of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO sample exhibited thin and transparent properties. The few-layer characteristic of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO is also observed in HRTEM (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>f) with a larger interspace and smaller size. A layer spacing of 1.2 nm along the <i>c</i>-axis is consistent with the XRD results. Moreover, the corresponding selected area electron diffraction pattern (SAED) of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO showed that the basal planes’ hexagonal structure remained unchanged after HEMM treatment (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>f, inset). EDS elemental analysis was employed to study the elemental distribution in MXene samples. Atomic concentrations of Ti, F, O, and C elements on the surface of powdered samples are given in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/suppl_file/am7b12155_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>. The results indicate the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled sample has the highest oxygen concentration, further verifying the oxidation happened during HEMM treatment without the protection of DMSO. In addition, the presence of S element in f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO sample indicated the existence of sulfur-containing functional groups on Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> surface. As shown in FTIR spectrum, the bands at 1050, 664, and 592 cm<sup>–1</sup> are assigned to the sulfur-containing functional groups on the surface of MXene.</div><div class="NLM_p">The samples were further analyzed by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) to characterize the surface chemical composition. Ti, F, O, and C elements are detected in survey spectra of MXene samples (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>g, Figure <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/suppl_file/am7b12155_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S5</a>). High-resolution XPS spectra of Ti 2p and C 1s core levels of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled, and f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO samples are shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>a–f. High-resolution Ti 2p and C 1s spectra of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled and f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO samples are similar to Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF sample, with the differences in concentration for different components. The Ti 2p core level is fitted with three doublets (Ti 2p<sub>3/2</sub>–Ti 2p<sub>1/2</sub>). The Ti 2p<sub>3/2</sub> components were located at 455.9, 457.4, and 458.8 eV, respectively. The dominant Ti 2p<sub>3/2</sub> component located at 458.8 eV is associated with Ti ions with a formal valence +4, together with the Ti 2p<sub>1/2</sub> peak at 464.7 eV, confirm TiO<sub>2</sub> in all samples due to the oxidation happening during the XPS analysis. The Ti 2p<sub>3/2</sub> component located at 455.9 eV corresponds to Ti–C bond. This component shows an obvious decline after HEMM treatment without the protection of DMSO solvent in Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled sample. The Ti 2p<sub>3/2</sub> component located at 457.4 eV can be assigned to Ti–X peak with a combination of substoichiometric TiC<sub><i>x</i></sub> (<i>x</i> &lt; 1) and TiC<sub><i>x</i></sub>O<sub><i>y</i></sub>. The C 1s core level of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled, and f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO samples are fitted using four components located at 281.8, 284.8, 286.4, and 288.9 eV, corresponding to C–Ti, C–C, C–Ti–O, and C–F bonds, respectively. The components corresponding to C–Ti and C–Ti–O were nearly absent in the high-resolution C 1s spectra of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled, which has the highest C–C bond component concentration. In addition, the signals of S element appeared in the survey XPS spectra of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO sample (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>g). The chemical state was identified by the high-resolution S 2p spectrum (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>h). The S 2p spectrum exhibits four peaks at a binding energy at 161.5, 164.8, 166.5, and 168.4 eV, respectively. The S<sup>2–</sup> species (161.5 and 164.8 eV) predominate on the surface of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO sample. It has been reported that the S 2p<sub>3/2</sub> peak at 161.5 eV combined with the Ti 2p<sub>3/2</sub> peak at 457 eV are assigned to Ti–S bond, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42 ref43'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42 ref43" aria-label="reference 42 and 43">(42, 43)</a> which indicates the substitution of Ti–OH/Ti–O groups by S (or S<sup>2–</sup>) groups on the surface of MXene during the HEMM treatment with DMSO. The nonequilibrium features (high temperature and oxygen-poor atmosphere induced by HEMM treatment) and high loosely packed surface state of few-layer MXene facilitates S-containing functional groups attached on the surface of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO. Quantitative analysis shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>i implies the concentration of S element in f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO is 2.56%.</div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/medium/am-2017-121554_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/large/am-2017-121554_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. High-resolution Ti 2p and C 1s spectra of (a–d) Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF, (b–e) f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO, and (c–f) Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled, respectively; (g) XPS survey spectra of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T_DMSO; (h) high-resolution S 2p spectra of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO; (i) atomic ratio of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/large/am-2017-121554_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b12155&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Nitrogen adsorption–desorption isotherm analysis was further characterized to evaluate the specific surface area and pore structure of the samples. As shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig4" aria-label="Figure 4">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>a, f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO sample exhibits a typical IV isotherm curve with a distinct hysteresis loop of type H3 in the medium-/high-pressure region (0.7 &lt; <i>P</i>/<i>P</i><sub>0</sub> &lt; 1), indicating the existence of mesopores and interconnected macropores. The specific surface is calculated to be 52.38 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>–1</sup>, which is much higher than that of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF (3.45 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>–1</sup>) and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled (9.32 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>–1</sup>). The pore size distribution calculated by desorption isotherms using Barret–Joyner–Halenda (BJH) method is shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig4" aria-label="Figure 4">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>b. The pore volume of the f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO sample (0.205 cm<sup>3</sup> g<sup>–1</sup>) is also greatly larger than Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF (0.026 cm<sup>3</sup> g<sup>–1</sup>), resulting in sufficient electrolyte uptake for fast ionic transport.The f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO with the tremendous increase in surface area is expected to enhance ion conductivity.</div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/medium/am-2017-121554_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/large/am-2017-121554_0004.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. (a) Nitrogen adsorption–desorption isotherms and (b) pore size distributions of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled, and f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO samples.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/large/am-2017-121554_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b12155&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The electrochemical properties of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled, and f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO electrodes were characterized by cyclic voltammetry (CV) and galvanostatic charge–discharge cycling in a two-electrode cell using Na foil as both counter and reference electrode. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>a shows the initial five CV curves of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO electrode in the range of 0.01–3.0 V at a scan rate of 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. The CV scan for f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO electrode is not quite different from the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF electrode. A pair of broad cathodic/anodic peaks located at around 0.6/1.0 V can be observed to be associated with Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction from f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO electrode, which is consistent with previous reported pristine MXene. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref44" aria-label="reference 44">(44)</a> A small reduction peak at 1.05 V was observed in the second and following cycles, suggesting a reaction between S and Na. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref45" aria-label="reference 45">(45)</a> The dominant irreversible cathodic peak located at nearly 0.5 V in the first cathodic sweep can be commonly assigned to irreversible side reactions on the surface of electrodes, including the formation of a solid–electrolyte interface (SEI) layer, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46 ref47 ref48'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref46 ref47 ref48" aria-label="reference 46 to 48">(46-48)</a> and possible reaction between Na<sup>+</sup> and surface functional groups of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>. A similar phenomenon was reported previously in MXene-based and other 2D materials for Li and Na storage. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19 ref24 ref34 ref35 ref36 ref49'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19 ref24 ref34 ref35 ref36 ref49" aria-label="reference 19, 24, 34 to 36 and 49">(19, 24, 34-36, 49)</a> The f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO electrode in the initial cycle showed a discharge and charge specific capacity of 520 and 267 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at a current density of 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup> (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>b). Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled electrodes delivered low capacities of 220 and 120 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at the same current density. The initial Coulombic efficiency of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO is relatively lower than pristine MXene because of a higher surface area exposed in electrolyte, in good agreement with previous reported few- and single-layer Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29" aria-label="reference 29">(29)</a> After 500 cycles, a reversible capacity of 196 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> is achieved in f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO at a current density of 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, which is nearly 2 times higher than that of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled electrodes (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>c). Compared with stacked MXene, the expanded interlayer spacing of few-layer MXene with a smaller size and an increased active surface area further enhances both electronic and ionic conductivity. The f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO electrode also showed the greatest capacity retention compared with the reported single- and/or few-layer MXene electrodes in SIBs (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/suppl_file/am7b12155_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">TableS2</a>). <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>d shows the rate capabilities of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled, and f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO electrodes. A reversible capacity of 110 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> can still be achieved at a high rate up to 2 A g<sup>–1</sup>. In contrast, very limited capacity of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled electrodes can be retained at high rates. The combination of electrolyte accessible area and electrical conductivity of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO electrode leads to such high rate capability. In addition, the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMF and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_EtOH electrodes also exhibited the higher capacities than Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/suppl_file/am7b12155_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>. The electrochemical performances of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO are superior to other solvent-treated MXenes, suggesting that the most efficient delamination is achieved by using DMSO.</div><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/medium/am-2017-121554_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/large/am-2017-121554_0005.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. Electrochemical performances of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF, f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO, and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled electrodes for SIBs. (a) CV curves of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO electrode at a scan rate of 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>; (b) galvanostatic charge–discharge profiles for the first cycle at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> in 0.01–2.5 V; (c) cycling performance at a current of 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>; (d) rate performance; (e) ultralong cycle life of 1500 cycles achieved by f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO at a current rate of 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/asset/images/large/am-2017-121554_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b12155&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p last">The structural stability of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO is also verified by TEM after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. The few-layer structure can be seen clearly in TEM image of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/suppl_file/am7b12155_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7a, b</a>), while the single-layer MXenes obtained by liquid delamination always inevitably restack together causing a degradation of the specific capacity and high rate performance. Notably, a reversible capacity of 76 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after an exceptionally long lifetime of 1500 cycles is achieved at very high current density of 1 A g<sup>–1</sup> (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>e). Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) was used to explore the charge transfer and ion transport within different electrodes and the Nyquist plots were shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/suppl_file/am7b12155_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S8</a>. All EIS curves can be divided into two regions with a semicircle in high-frequency region and inclined line in the low-frequency region. The diameter of semicircle of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO is much smaller than Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled, demonstrating a low charge-transfer impedance. Moreover, f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO electrode has the higher slope in the low-frequency region among three different electrodes, indicating a lower diffusion resistance and better kinetics compared to pristine Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_HF and Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_milled. Owing to the few-layer structure, the contact area between electrode and electrolyte will be increased, leading to a much more effective electrochemical reaction interface.</div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">Conclusion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In summary, through a novel HEMM method with DMSO as solvent and intercalator, f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO can be prepared in large scale and high stability. The f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO with larger interlayer space, smaller size, and modified surface retains 2D layered morphology, and provides maximum access of electrolyte to electrodes. In contrast, the HEMM treatment without the protection of DMSO promotes the transformation from Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> to TiO<sub>2</sub> and carbon. The f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO electrode exhibits a good reversible capacity of 267 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, which is much higher than pristine MXene. A stable capacity of 196 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> can be achieved in f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO electrode after 500 cycles. Note that a greatly enhanced rate performance is observed; a high capacity of 110 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> can be achieved at high current density of 2 A g<sup>–1</sup>, making the f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO electrode a more desirable anode for SIBs. This low-cost and scalable synthetic route also could be extended to other delaminated MXenes materials for application in energy storage, catalysis, sensors, and beyond.</div></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i4">Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec4_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5"> Synthesis of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub></h3><div class="NLM_p last">Two-dimensional titanium carbide Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> was synthesized by exfoliating commercial Ti<sub>3</sub>AlC<sub>2</sub> powders (&gt;98 wt % purity) with similar procedures reported by Naguib et al. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18" aria-label="reference 18">(18)</a> The Ti<sub>3</sub>AlC<sub>2</sub> powder was immersed in 49% HF solution by stirring for 18 h at room temperature. The resulting powder was rinsed by deionized water several times to remove the residual HF and impurities until the pH is 5–6. The obtained wet sediments were then dried in a vacuum oven at 80 °C overnight.</div></div><div id="sec4_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6"> Synthesis of f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO was prepared via a high-energy mechanical-milling method with a planetary ball-mill apparatus (Fritsch Pulverisette 6). One gram of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> powder was immersed in 30 mL of DMSO solvent poured in a hardened stainless steel vial (80 cm<sup>3</sup>) with hardened steel balls with a ball-to-powder weight ratio of 20:1. The HEMM was conducted with a rotation speed of 400 rpm for 12 h. The resulting powders were washed with absolute ethanol and acetone several times, and then dried at 60 °C for 12 h. The as-prepared f-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>_DMSO was next annealed at 400 °C in N<sub>2</sub> for 2 h to remove residual solvent. The average yield of few-layer MXene per batch is about 0.8 g with 1 g of multilayer MXene input. For comparison, milled Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> sample was also prepared under similar conditions with other organic solvents (<i>N</i>,<i>N</i>-dimethylformamide, ethanol) and without organic solvents.</div></div><div id="sec4_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i7" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i7"> Materials Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The crystal structure of the obtained sample was characterized by the Bruker D8 advanced powder diffractometer with Cu Kα radiation (λ ∼ 0.15406) ranging from 5° to 80°. XPS analysis was performed in PerkinElmer PHI 550 spectrometer with Al Kα (1486.6 eV) as the X-ray source. The morphologies and microstructural properties were characterized by field-emission scanning electron microscopy (FESEM, JSM-6080LV), transmission electron microscopy (TEM, FEI,Tecnai20), and high-resolution transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM, JEM-2100). The elemental analysis was performed on an energy dispersive X-ray spectrometer (EDS) attached to the HRTEM instrument. The Raman spectra were recorded on a WITEC-CRM Raman system (WITEC, Germany), using 532 nm laser (2.33 eV) as the excitation source. BET surface area of the samples was determined using a surface area analyzer (Micromeitics ASAP 2420) at 77 K.</div></div><div id="sec4_4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i8" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i8"> Electrochemical Measurements</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The electrochemical measurements were carried out using standard CR2032-type coin cell with sodium pellets as the counter and the reference electrode. The working electrodes were prepared by slurry coating procedure. The slurry consisted of 80 wt % active material, 10 wt % acetylene black and 10 wt % carboxymethyl cellulose (CMC) dissolved in water was uniformly spread onto a carbon coated copper foil. Afterward, the electrode was dried at 70 °C under vacuum overnight. The average mass loading of electrodes is about 1 mg on Cu foil (12 mm in diameter).The electrolyte was 1 M NaClO<sub>4</sub> dissolved in ethylene carbonate/polycarbonate (EC/PC, 1:1 by vol.) with 5 wt % fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) additive, and the glass microfiber (Whatman GD/F) used as separators. All the cells were assembled in an argon-filled glovebox with water/oxygen content lower than 1 ppm. Galvanostatic discharge/charge tests were conducted on a LAND 2001A battery Tester with a cutoff voltage range of 0.01–2.5 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>. Cyclic voltammetry measurements were performed on a CHI660C electrochemical workstation.</div></div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i9">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.7b12155" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.7b12155</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">XRD patterns; SEM and TEM images; FTIR spectrum; XPS survey spectra; charge–discharge profiles; TEM images after 100 cycles; electrochemical impedance spectra; atomic concentration (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/suppl_file/am7b12155_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b12155/suppl_file/am7b12155_si_001.pdf">am7b12155_si_001.pdf (2.16 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.7b12155" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">
