                        cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Universal quinone electrodes for long cycle life aqueous rechargeable batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Yanliang; Jing, Yan; Gheytani, Saman; Lee, Kuan-Yi; Liu, Ping; Facchetti, Antonio; Yao, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">841-848</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Aq. rechargeable batteries provide the safety, robustness, affordability, and environmental friendliness necessary for grid storage and elec. vehicle operations, but their adoption is plagued by poor cycle life due to the structural and chem. instability of the anode materials.  We report quinones as stable anode materials by exploiting their structurally stable ion-coordination charge storage mechanism and chem. inertness towards aq. electrolytes.  Upon rational selection/design of quinone structures, we demonstrate three systems that coupled with industrially established cathodes and electrolytes exhibit long cycle life (≤3000 cycles/3500 h), fast kinetics (≥20C), high anode specific capacity (up to 200-395 mAh/g), and several examples of state-of-the-art specific energy/energy d. (up to 76-92 Wh/Kg/161-208 Wh/L) for several operational pH values (-1 to 15), charge carrier species (H+, Li+, Na+, K+, Mg2+), temp. (-35 to 25 °C), and atm. (with/without O), making them a universal anode approach for any aq. battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqqJvJ0f0r-ErVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhys2j3CWEeXA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtVWmtL%252FO&amp;md5=1b8a257461807b1762785be2efb01533</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1038/nature16484"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jung Lee, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chun Lau, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Asadi, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H. H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Brombosz, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhai, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Miller, D. J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sub Jeong, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, J.                         cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A lithium-oxygen battery based on lithium superoxide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Jun; Jung Lee, Yun; Luo, Xiangyi; Chun Lau, Kah; Asadi, Mohammad; Wang, Hsien-Hau; Brombosz, Scott; Wen, Jianguo; Zhai, Dengyun; Chen, Zonghai; Miller, Dean J.; Sub Jeong, Yo; Park, Jin-Bum; Zak Fang, Zhigang; Kumar, Bijandra; Salehi-Khojin, Amin; Sun, Yang-Kook; Curtiss, Larry A.; Amine, Khalil</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature (London, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">529</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7586</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">377-382</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Batteries based on Na superoxide and on K superoxide have recently been reported.  However, there have been no reports of a battery based on Li superoxide (LiO2), despite much research into the Li-O battery because of its potential high energy d.  Several studies of Li-O2 batteries found evidence of LiO2 being formed as one component of the discharge product along with Li peroxide (Li2O2).  Theor. calcns. indicated that some forms of LiO2 may have a long lifetime.  Also probably it might should be possible to form LiO2 alone for use in a battery.  However, solid LiO2 was difficult to synthesize in pure form because it is thermodynamically unstable with respect to disproportionation, giving Li2O2.  Cryst. LiO2 can be stabilized in a Li-O2 battery by using a suitable graphene-based cathode.  Various characterization techniques reveal no evidence for the presence of Li2O2.  A novel templating growth mechanism involving the use of Ir nanoparticles on the cathode surface may be responsible for the growth of cryst. LiO2.  The LiO2 formed in the Li-O2 battery is stable enough for the battery to be repeatedly charged and discharged with a very low charge potential (∼3.2 V).  The authors anticipate that this discovery will lead to methods of synthesizing and stabilizing LiO2, which could open the way to high-energy-d. batteries based on LiO2 as well as to other possible uses of this compd., such as O storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqukDX2s3CJWbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljilhEK26D-5g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xns1Glsg%253D%253D&amp;md5=1a69e9df185320799927c776c22c5980</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms6693"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhan, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lei, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kropf, A.                         cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effectively suppressing dissolution of manganese from spinel lithium manganate via a nanoscale surface-doping approach</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Jun; Zhan, Chun; Wu, Tianpin; Wen, Jianguo; Lei, Yu; Kropf, A. Jeremy; Wu, Huiming; Miller, Dean J.; Elam, Jeffrey W.; Sun, Yang-Kook; Qiu, Xinping; Amine, Khalil</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The capacity fade of lithium manganate-based cells is assocd. with the dissoln. of Mn from cathode/electrolyte interface due to the disproportionation reaction of Mn(III), and the subsequent deposition of Mn(II) on the anode.  Suppressing the dissoln. of Mn from the cathode is crit. to reducing capacity fade of LiMn2O4-based cells.  Here we report a nanoscale surface-doping approach that minimizes Mn dissoln. from lithium manganate.  This approach exploits advantages of both bulk doping and surface-coating methods by stabilizing surface crystal structure of lithium manganate through cationic doping while maintaining bulk lithium manganate structure, and protecting bulk lithium manganate from electrolyte corrosion while maintaining ion and charge transport channels on the surface through the electrochem. active doping layer.  Consequently, the surface-doped lithium manganate demonstrates enhanced electrochem. performance.  This study provides encouraging evidence that surface doping could be a promising alternative to improve the cycling performance of lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqnuwX-deBZk7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljilhEK26D-5g"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mesoporous Silicon Anodes by Using Polybenzimidazole Derived Pyrrolic N-Enriched Carbon toward High-Energy Li-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nie, Ping; Liu, Xiaoyan; Fu, Ruirui; Wu, Yuting; Jiang, Jiangmin; Dou, Hui; Zhang, Xiaogang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The silicon anode holds great potential for next-generation lithium-ion batteries in view of its high gravimetric capacity and natural abundance.  The main challenges assocd. with silicon are the structural degrdn. and instability caused by huge vol. change upon cycling.  We report herein polybenzimidazole (PBI) derived pyrrolic N-enriched carbon as an ideal encapsulation onto microsized silicon spheres, which is achieved by an aerosol-assisted assembly combined with a simple physisorption process.  The new polymer derived carbon endows silicon with the structural and compositional characteristics of intrinsic high electronic cond., abundant pyrrolic nitrogen, and structure robustness.  The resulting mesoporous Si-PBI carbon composite exhibits excellent lithium storage performance in terms of high reversible specific capacity of 2172 mAh g-1, superior rate capability (1186 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1), and prolonged cycling life.  As a result, a fabricated Si/LiCoO2 full battery demonstrates high energy d. of 367 Wh kg-1 as well as good cycling stability for 100 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoIbFwYL9zaKbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljilhEK26D-5g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXntVajt78%253D&amp;md5=bfe953cc924e3a3c471939bc29b5aab8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1039/C6EE01807F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yi, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Advances in Titanium-Based Electrode Materials for Stationary Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent advances in titanium-based electrode materials for stationary sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Shaohua; Yi, Jin; Sun, Yang; Zhou, Haoshen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, the attention to sodium-ion batteries has been refocused on large-scale energy storage applications, due to sodium's low cost and infinite abundance.  Sodium is one of the most abundant elements on earth and exhibits chem. properties similar to lithium.  Owing to their superior sodium storage capability esp. for excellent safety and stability, Ti-based compds. have been extensively investigated as both cathode and anode materials.  Herein we outline the current cathodes and anodes, and emphasize the crit. roles of titanium in developing advanced electrodes for sodium-ion batteries.  The latest advances and progress in the exploration of Ti-based compds. with various different frameworks such as NASICON, tunnel, MXenes, spinel, and layered structures are systematically reviewed.  The straightforward linking of the structure-function-property relationship for Ti-based compds., esp. for layered Na/Ti-contg. oxides, is summarized and analyzed.  The titanium element plays a crit. role in both pos. and neg. electrodes, i.e., supplying the charge transfer and high safety for anodes and greatly enhancing the structural and cycling stability for cathodes.  Based on the bi-functional roles of titanium, a new concept of sym. Na-ion cells employing layered Na/Ti-contg. oxides as bipolar electrodes is proposed and realized.  Sym. Na-ion cells already offered a high voltage and withstood long time charge-discharge processes, demonstrating the practicality beyond the proof of concept.  The participation of titanium in sodium-based electrode materials will greatly promote the development of room-temp. sodium-ion batteries towards stationary energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrWmTGIPGjjUbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljilhEK26D-5g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtlOns7nL&amp;md5=5c9fbf39a0d13dfe65a745d3e501da55</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2016.12.005"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yao, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, J.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mesoporous single-crystal-like TiO2 mesocages threaded with carbon nanotubes for high-performance electrochemical energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Peng, Yiting; Le, Zaiyuan; Wen, Meicheng; Zhang, Dieqing; Chen, Zheng; Wu, Hao Bin; Li, Hexing; Lu, Yunfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel nanocomposite based on mesoporous single-cryst. TiO2 particles (TiO2 mesocages) threaded with carbon nanotubes (CNTs) has been successfully synthesized via a facile solvothermal method.  The unique hybrid architecture endows the nanocomposite with facile ion and electron transport pathways, abundant active surface sites and high structure robustness.  As a result, remarkable electrochem. lithium storage properties in terms of high capacity, excellent rate capability and ultra-stable long-term cycling performance have been achieved by the CNTs-threaded TiO2 mesocages.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo2sMHhFDdXDbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgOLLYoYk_jiQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkslOjsrs%253D&amp;md5=2637e28ce51bae2f5178b5f83933d423</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.6b08332"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Le, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nie, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bian, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, H.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitive Sodium Storage in Mesoporous Single-Crystal-like TiO2-Graphene Nanocomposite Enables High-Performance Sodium-Ion Capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Le, Zaiyuan; Liu, Fang; Nie, Ping; Li, Xinru; Liu, Xiaoyan; Bian, Zhenfeng; Chen, Gen; Wu, Hao Bin; Lu, Yunfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion capacitors can potentially combine the virtues of high power capability of conventional electrochem. capacitors and high energy d. of batteries.  However, the lack of high-performance electrode materials has been the major challenge of sodium-based energy storage devices.  We report a microwave-assisted synthesis of single-crystal-like anatase TiO2 mesocages anchored on graphene as a sodium storage material.  The architecture of the nanocomposite results in pseudocapacitive charge storage behavior with fast kinetics, high reversibility, and negligible degrdn. to the micro/nanostructure.  The nanocomposite delivers a high capacity of 268 mAh/g at 0.2 C, which remains 126 mAh/g at 10 C for over 18,000 cycles.  Coupling with a C-based cathode, a full cell of sodium-ion capacitor successfully demonstrates a high energy d. of 64.2 Wh/Kg at 56.3 W/Kg and 25.8 Wh/Kg at 1357 W/Kg, as well as an ultralong lifespan of 10,000 cycles with over 90% of capacity retention.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrefz1bcMVcvLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgOLLYoYk_jiQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Prussian Blue Analogue with Fast Kinetics Through Electronic Coupling for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nie, Ping; Yuan, Jiaren; Wang, Jie; Le, Zaiyuan; Xu, Guiyin; Hao, Liang; Pang, Gang; Wu, Yuting; Dou, Hui; Yan, Xiaohong; Zhang, Xiaogang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Alternative battery systems based on the chem. of sodium are being considered to offer sustainability and cost-effectiveness.  Herein, a simple and new method is demonstrated to enable nickel hexacyanoferrate (NiHCF) Prussian blue analogs (PBA) nanocrystals to be an excellent host for sodium ion storage by functionalization with redox guest mol.  The method is achieved by using NiHCF PBA powders infiltrated with the 7,7,8,8-tetracyanoquinododimethane (TCNQ) soln.  Exptl. and ab initio calcns. results suggest that TCNQ mol. bridging with Fe atoms in NiHCF Prussian blue analog leads to electronic coupling between TCNQ mols. and NiHCF open-framework, which functions as an elec. highway for electron motion and cond. enhancement.  Combining the merits including high electronic cond., open framework structure, nanocrystal, and interconnected mesopores, the NiHCF/TCNQ shows high specific capacity, fast kinetics and good cycling stability, delivering a high specific capacity of 35 mAh g-1 after 2000 cycles, corresponding to a capacity loss of 0.035% decay per cycle.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo1ZoSLgniDgrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgOLLYoYk_jiQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXptFemsb4%253D&amp;md5=41bd1c1f15b9b11770afa438576a30d5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201400554"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Allen, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Raju, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Organic Pigment as a High-Performance Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv. B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Acc. Chem.                 10.1021/acs.accounts.5b00482</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D49%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D231-240%26journal%3DAcc.%2BChem.%2BRes.%26author%3DW.%2BLuo%26author%3DF.%2BShen%26author%3DC.%2BBommier%26author%3DH.%2BL.%2BZhu%26author%3DX.%2BL.%2BJi%26author%3DL.%2BB.%2BHu%26title%3DNa-Ion%2BBattery%2BAnodes%253A%2BMaterials%2Band%2BElectrochemistry%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.accounts.5b00482&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b12155&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.accounts.5b00482&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wei; Shen, Fei; Bommier, Clement; Zhu, Hongli; Ji, Xiulei; Hu, Liangbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">231-240</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACHRE4</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0001-4842</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The intermittent nature of renewable energy sources, such as solar and wind, calls for sustainable elec. energy storage (EES) technologies for stationary applications.  Li will be simply too rare for Li-ion batteries (LIBs) to be used for large-scale storage purposes.  In contrast, Na-ion batteries (NIBs) are highly promising to meet the demand of grid-level storage because Na is truly earth abundant and ubiquitous around the globe.  Furthermore, NIBs share a similar rocking-chair operation mechanism with LIBs, which potentially provides high reversibility and long cycling life.  It would be most efficient to transfer knowledge learned on LIBs during the last three decades to the development of NIBs.  Following this logic, rapid progress has been made in NIB cathode materials, where layered metal oxides and polyanionic compds. exhibit encouraging results.  On the anode side, pure graphite as the std. anode for LIBs can only form NaC64 in NIBs if solvent co-intercalation does not occur due to the unfavorable thermodn.  In fact, it was the utilization of a carbon anode in LIBs that enabled the com. successes.  Anodes of metal-ion batteries det. key characteristics, such as safety and cycling life; thus, it is indispensable to identify suitable anode materials for NIBs.In this Account, we review recent development on anode materials for NIBs.  Due to the limited space, we will mainly discuss carbon-based and alloy-based anodes and highlight progress made in our groups in this field.  We first present what is known about the failure mechanism of graphite anode in NIBs.  We then go on to discuss studies on hard carbon anodes, alloy-type anodes, and org. anodes.  Esp., the multiple functions of natural cellulose that is used as a low-cost carbon precursor for mass prodn. and as a soft substrate for tin anodes are highlighted.  The strategies of minimizing the surface area of carbon anodes for improving the first-cycle Coulombic efficiency are also outlined, where graphene oxide was employed as dehydration agent and 2,2,6,6-tetramethylpiperidine-1-oxyl (TEMPO) was used to unzip wood fiber.  Furthermore, surface modification by at. layer deposition technol. is introduced, where we discover that a thin layer of Al2O3 can function to encapsulate Sn nanoparticles, leading to a much enhanced cycling performance.  We also highlight recent work about the phosphorene/graphene anode, which outperformed other anodes in terms of capacity.  The arom. org. anode is also studied as anode with very high initial sodiation capacity.  Furthermore, electrochem. intercalation of Na ions into reduced graphene oxide is applied for fabricating transparent conductors, demonstrating the great feasibility of Na ion intercalation for optical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGorKnQvVSK3P7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgOLLYoYk_jiQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVGksrg%253D&amp;md5=90d2907a2b33fdcf59913255073dd969</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201410174"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Garsuch, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nazar, L. F.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sulfur Cathodes Based on Conductive MXene Nanosheets for High-Performance Lithium-Sulfur Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sulfur Cathodes Based on Conductive MXene Nanosheets for High-Performance Lithium-Sulfur Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Xiao; Garsuch, Arnd; Nazar, Linda F.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">54</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3907-3911</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Li-S batteries are amongst the most promising candidates to satisfy emerging energy-storage demands.  Suppression of the polysulfide shuttle while maintaining high S content is the main challenge that faces their practical development.  Here, the authors report that 2-dimensional early-transition-metal carbide conductive MXene phases-reported to be impressive supercapacitor materials-also perform as excellent S battery hosts owing to their inherently high underlying metallic cond. and self-functionalized surfaces.  The 70% S/Ti2C composites exhibit stable long-term cycling performance because of strong interaction of the polysulfide species with the surface Ti atoms, demonstrated by XPS studies.  The cathodes show excellent cycling performance with specific capacity close to 1200 mA-h g-1 at a 5-h charge/discharge (C/5) current rate.  Capacity retention of 80% is achieved over 400 cycles at a 2-h charge/discharge (C/2) current rate.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGogPhjJ6nEXvbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgOLLYoYk_jiQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sn4+ Ion Decorated Highly Conductive Ti3C2 MXene: Promising Lithium-Ion Anodes with Enhanced Volumetric Capacity and Cyclic Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Jianmin; Tao, Xinyong; Zhang, Jun; Xia, Yang; Huang, Hui; Zhang, Liyuan; Gan, Yongping; Liang, Chu; Zhang, Wenkui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2491-2499</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional transition metal carbide materials called MXenes show potential application for energy storage due to their remarkable elec. cond. and low Li+ diffusion barrier.  However, the lower capacity of MXene anodes limits their further application in lithium-ion batteries.  Herein, with inspiration from the unique metal ion uptake behavior of highly conductive Ti3C2 MXene, we overcome this impediment by fabricating Sn4+ ion decorated Ti3C2 nanocomposites (PVP-Sn(IV)@Ti3C2) via a facile polyvinylpyrrolidone (PVP)-assisted liq.-phase immersion process.  An amorphous Sn(IV) nanocomplex, about 6-7 nm in lateral size, has been homogeneously anchored on the surface of alk-Ti3C2 matrix by ion-exchange and electrostatic interactions.  In addn., XRD and TEM results demonstrate the successful insertion of Sn4+ into the interlamination of an alkalization-intercalated Ti3C2 (alk-Ti3C2) matrix.  Due to the possible "pillar effect" of Sn between layers of alk-Ti3C2 and the synergistic effect between the alk-Ti3C2 matrix and Sn, the nanocomposites exhibit a superior reversible volumetric capacity of 1375 mAh cm-3 (635 mAh g-1) at 216.5 mA cm-3 (100 mA g-1), which is significantly higher than that of a graphite electrode (550 mAh cm-3), and show excellent cycling stability after 50 cycles.  Even at a high c.d. of 6495 mA cm-3 (3 A g-1), these nanocomposites retain a stable specific capacity of 504.5 mAh cm-3 (233 mAh g-1).  These results demonstrate that PVP-Sn(IV)@Ti3C2 nanocomposites offer fascinating potential for high-performance lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqMbcMPHPZiqrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhuJNXHPaKwwA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhvV2murg%253D&amp;md5=7e89aed949a012eb8ef6a739def7eaff</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1016/j.elecom.2012.01.002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Naguib, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Come, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dyatkin, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Presser, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Taberna, P.                 10.1016/j.elecom.2012.01.002</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D16%26publication_year%3D2012%26pages%3D61-64%26journal%3DElectrochem.%2BCommun.%26author%3DM.%2BNaguib%26author%3DJ.%2BCome%26author%3DB.%2BDyatkin%26author%3DV.%2BPresser%26author%3DP.%2BL.%2BTaberna%26author%3DP.%2BSimon%26author%3DM.%2BW.%2BBarsoum%26author%3DY.%2BGogotsi%26title%3DMXene%253A%2BA%2BPromising%2BTransition%2BMetal%2BCarbide%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BLithium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.elecom.2012.01.002&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b12155&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.elecom.2012.01.002&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MXene: a promising transition metal carbide anode for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Naguib, Michael; Come, Jeremy; Dyatkin, Boris; Presser, Volker; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Simon, Patrice; Barsoum, Michel W.; Gogotsi, Yury</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochemistry Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">61-64</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein we report on Li insertion into a new two-dimensional (2-D) layered Ti2C-based material (MXene) with an oxidized surface, formed by etching Al from Ti2AlC in HF at room temp.  Nitrogen sorption of treated powders showed desorption hysteresis consistent with the presence of slit-like pores.  At 23 m2 g- 1, the sp. surface area was an order of magnitude higher than untreated Ti2AlC.  Cyclic voltammetry exhibited lithiation and delithiation peaks at 1.6 V and 2 V vs. Li+/Li, resp.  At C/25, the steady state capacity was 225 mAh g- 1; at 1C, it was 110 mAh g- 1 after 80 cycles; at 3C, it was 80 mAh g- 1 after 120 cycles; at 10C, it was 70 mAh g- 1 after 200 cycles.  Since Ti2C is a member of the MXene family - where M is an early transition metal and X is C and/or N - that to date includes Ti3C2, Ta4C3, TiNbC, and (V0.5,Cr0.5)3C2, our results suggest that MXenes are promising as anode materials for Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr3daD07p4pqrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhuJNXHPaKwwA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XitFOhuro%253D&amp;md5=64431e9e2cd84fab02660a141adfbc91</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.02.043"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ahmed, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Anjum, D. H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gogotsi, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Alshareef, H. N.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Atomic Layer Deposition of SnO<sub>2</sub> on MXene for Li-Ion Battery Anodes</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Energy</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">34</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">249</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">256</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atomic layer deposition of SnO2 on MXene for Li-ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ahmed, Bilal; Anjum, Dalaver H.; Gogotsi, Yury; Alshareef, Husam N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">34</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">249-256</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this report, we show that oxide battery anodes can be grown on two-dimensional titanium carbide sheets (MXenes) by at. layer deposition.  Using this approach, we have fabricated a composite SnO2/MXene anode for Li-ion battery applications.  The SnO2/MXene anode exploits the high Li-ion capacity offered by SnO2, while maintaining the structural and mech. integrity of the conductive MXene platform.  The at. layer deposition (ALD) conditions used to deposit SnO2 on MXene terminated with oxygen, fluorine, and hydroxyl-groups were found to be crit. for preventing MXene degrdn. during ALD.  We demonstrate that SnO2/MXene electrodes exhibit excellent electrochem. performance as Li-ion battery anodes, where conductive MXene sheets act to buffer the vol. changes assocd. with lithiation and delithiation of SnO2.  The cyclic performance of the anodes is further improved by depositing a very thin passivation layer of HfO2, in the same ALD reactor, on the SnO2/MXene anode.  This is shown by high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy to also improve the structural integrity of the SnO2/MXene anode during cycling.  The HfO2 coated SnO2/MXene electrodes demonstrate a stable specific capacity of 843 mAh/g when used as Li-ion battery anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrmEJQpPWXc8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhuJNXHPaKwwA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXjs1Ogs7g%253D&amp;md5=282fdb82c8a86b5acf6c4ece2bbbb45b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1007/s11467-015-0493-x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lei, J.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical performance of Ti3C2 supercapacitors in KOH electrolyte</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gao, Yupeng; Wang, Libo; Li, Zhengyang; Zhang, Yafei; Xing, Baolin; Zhang, Chuanxiang; Zhou, Aiguo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Advanced Ceramics</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional (2D) carbide Ti3C2 was synthesized by exfoliating Ti3AlC2 in HF soln. and used for supercapacitive performance investigation in 3 M KOH electrolyte.  The sp. surface area (SSA) of as-synthesized Ti3C2 was 22.35 m2/g.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two-Dimensional Nanocrystals Produced by Exfoliation of Ti3AlC2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Naguib, Michael; Kurtoglu, Murat; Presser, Volker; Lu, Jun; Niu, Junjie; Heon, Min; Hultman, Lars; Gogotsi, Yury; Barsoum, Michel W.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">23</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4248-4253</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Treatment of Ti3AlC2 powders for 2 h in HF results in the formation of exfoliated 2-dimensional (2D) Ti3C2 layers (nanosheets).  The Ti3AlC2 structure is composed of individual Ti3C2 layers sepd. by Al atoms.  Upon reaction with HF, Al atoms are removed from between the layers, resulting in the exfoliation of individual Ti3C2 layers from each other due to the loss of metallic bonding holding them together when the Al atoms are present.  The exposed 2D Ti3C2 layers possess 2 exposed Ti atoms per unit formula that should be satisfied by suitable ligands.  Since the expts. were conducted in an aq. environment rich in F ions, hydroxyl and F are the most probable ligands.  Modeling of each case was conduced by attaching resp. ligands to the exposed Ti atoms followed by full geometry optimizations.  The exposed Ti surfaces appear to be terminated by OH and/or F.  The large elastic moduli predicted by ab initio simulation, and the possibility of varying their surface chem. render these nanosheets attractive as polymer composite fillers.  The implications and importance of this work extend far beyond the results shown herein.  There are over 60 currently known MAX phases; therefore, this work, in principle, opens the door for formation of a large no. of 2D Mn+1Xn structures, including the carbides and nitrides of Ti, V, Cr, Nb, Ta, Hf, and Zr.  The latter could include 2D structures of combination of M-atoms, e.g., Ti0.5Zr0.5InC and/or different combinations of C and N, such as Ti2AlC0.5N0.5, if the selective chem. etching is extended to other MAX phases.  We currently have solid evidence for the exfoliation of Ta4AlC3 into Ta4C3 flakes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpgGCYRpfKi4bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhuJNXHPaKwwA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interdiffusion Reaction-Assisted Hybridization of Two-Dimensional Metal-Organic Frameworks and Ti3C2Tx Nanosheets for Electrocatalytic Oxygen Evolution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Li; Dong, Biliang; Li, Shaozhou; Zhou, Lijun; Lai, Linfei; Wang, Zhiwei; Zhao, Shulin; Han, Min; Gao, Kai; Lu, Min; Xie, Xiaoji; Chen, Bo; Liu, Zhengdong; Wang, Xiangjing; Zhang, Hao; Li, Hai; Liu, Juqing; Zhang, Hua; Huang, Xiao; Huang, Wei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5800-5807</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional (2D) metal-org. framework (MOF) nanosheets were recently regarded as the model electrocatalysts due to their porous structure, fast mass and ion transfer through the thickness, and large portion of exposed active metal centers.  Combining them with elec. conductive 2-dimensional nanosheets is anticipated to achieve further improved performance in electrocatalysis.  The authors in situ hybridized 2-dimensional Co 1,4-benzenedicarboxylate (CoBDC) with Ti3C2Tx (the MXene phase) nanosheets via an interdiffusion reaction-assisted process.  The resulting hybrid material was applied in the O evolution reaction and achieved a c.d. of 10 mA cm-2 at a potential of 1.64 V vs. reversible H electrode and a Tafel slope of 48.2 mV dec-1 in 0.1M KOH.  These results outperform those obtained by the std. IrO2-based catalyst and are comparable with or even better than those achieved by the previously reported state-of-the-art transition-metal-based catalysts.  While the CoBDC layer provided the highly porous structure and large active surface area, the elec. conductive and hydrophilic Ti3C2Tx nanosheets enabled the rapid charge and ion transfer across the well-defined Ti3C2Tx-CoBDC interface and facilitated the access of aq. electrolyte to the catalytically active CoBDC surfaces.  The hybrid nanosheets were further fabricated into an air cathode for a rechargeable Zn-air battery, which was successfully used to power a light-emitting diode.  Probably the in situ hybridization of MXenes and 2-dimensional MOFs with interface control will provide more opportunities for their use in energy-based applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpKkccBy1HgubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifqWNYwWHtpw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXnvFCntb4%253D&amp;md5=b07ee56fa5c742aaa58c86749876e2da</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1021/ja501520b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Naguib, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mochalin, V.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Role of surface structure on Li-ion energy storage capacity of two-dimensional transition-metal carbides</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie, Yu; Naguib, Michael; Mochalin, Vadym N.; Barsoum, Michel W.; Gogotsi, Yury; Yu, Xiqian; Nam, Kyung-Wan; Yang, Xiao-Qing; Kolesnikov, Alexander I.; Kent, Paul R. C.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">136</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6385-6394</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A combination of d. functional theory (DFT) calcns. and expts. is used to shed light on the relation between surface structure and Li-ion storage capacities of the following functionalized two-dimensional (2D) transition-metal carbides or MXenes: Sc2C, Ti2C, Ti3C2, V2C, Cr2C, and Nb2C.  The Li-ion storage capacities are found to strongly depend on the nature of the surface functional groups, with O groups exhibiting the highest theor. Li-ion storage capacities.  MXene surfaces can be initially covered with OH groups, removable by high-temp. treatment or by reactions in the first lithiation cycle.  This was verified by annealing f-Nb2C and f-Ti3C2 at 673 and 773 K in vacuum for 40 h and in situ X-ray adsorption spectroscopy (XAS) and Li capacity measurements for the first lithiation/delithiation cycle of f-Ti3C2.  The high-temp. removal of water and OH was confirmed using X-ray diffraction and inelastic neutron scattering.  The voltage profile and X-ray adsorption near edge structure of f-Ti3C2 revealed surface reactions in the first lithiation cycle.  Moreover, lithiated oxygen terminated MXenes surfaces are able to adsorb addnl. Li beyond a monolayer, providing a mechanism to substantially increase capacity, as obsd. mainly in delaminated MXenes and confirmed by DFT calcns. and XAS.  The calcd. Li diffusion barriers are low, indicative of the measured high-rate performance.  We predict the not yet synthesized Cr2C to possess high Li capacity due to the low activation energy of water formation at high temp., while the not yet synthesized Sc2C is predicted to potentially display low Li capacity due to higher reaction barriers for OH removal.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqmrshuDbstirVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifqWNYwWHtpw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXltFGlsbk%253D&amp;md5=8a48485460db1c614d1ec6741da1120f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201609306"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ding, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Caro, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Two-Dimensional Lamellar Membrane: MXene Nanosheet Stacks</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Two-Dimensional Lamellar Membrane: MXene Nanosheet Stacks</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ding, Li; Wei, Yanying; Wang, Yanjie; Chen, Hongbin; Caro, Juergen; Wang, Haihui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional (2D) materials are promising candidates for advanced water purifn. membranes. Ti3C2Tx with the functional groups T (O, OH, and/or F) can be produced by etching and ultrasonication and stapled on a porous support by vacuum filtration.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors report a simple and scalable method to fabricate homogeneous transparent conductive thin films (Ti2CTx, one of the MXene) by dip coating of an Al2O3 substrate in a colloidal soln. of large-area Ti2CTx thin flakes.  SEM and at. force microscopy images exhibit the wafer-scale homogeneous Ti2CTx thin film (∼5 nm) covering the whole substrate.  The sheet resistance is ≥70 Ω/sq at 86% transmittance, which corresponds to the high figure of merit (FOM) of 40.7.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cation Intercalation and High Volumetric Capacitance of Two-Dimensional Titanium Carbide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lukatskaya, Maria R.; Mashtalir, Olha; Ren, Chang E.; Dall'Agnese, Yohan; Rozier, Patrick; Taberna, Pierre Louis; Naguib, Michael; Simon, Patrice; Barsoum, Michel W.; Gogotsi, Yury</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science (Washington, DC, United States)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The intercalation of ions into layered compds. has long been exploited in energy storage devices such as batteries and electrochem. capacitors.  However, few host materials are known for ions much larger than lithium.  We demonstrate the spontaneous intercalation of cations from aq. salt solns. between two-dimensional (2D) Ti3C2 MXene layers.  MXenes combine 2D conductive carbide layers with a hydrophilic, primarily hydroxyl-terminated surface.  A variety of cations, including Na+, K+, NH4+, Mg2+, and Al3+, can also be intercalated electrochem., offering capacitance in excess of 300 F per cubic centimeter (much higher than that of porous carbons).  This study provides a basis for exploring a large family of 2D carbides and carbonitrides in electrochem. energy storage applications using single- and multivalent ions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrqTYKv3tOPbrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifqWNYwWHtpw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsFSmsLjO&amp;md5=c700d741ed4085a1a8cb2cd6f3d30fac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.6b07668"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, J.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pillared Structure Design of MXene with Ultralarge Interlayer Spacing for High-Performance Lithium-Ion Capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Jianmin; Zhang, Wenkui; Yuan, Huadong; Jin, Chengbin; Zhang, Liyuan; Huang, Hui; Liang, Chu; Xia, Yang; Zhang, Jun; Gan, Yongping; Tao, Xinyong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional transition-metal carbide materials (termed MXene) have attracted huge attention in the field of electrochem. energy storage due to their excellent elec. cond., high volumetric capacity, etc.  Herein, with inspiration from the interesting structure of pillared interlayered clays, we attempt to fabricate pillared Ti3C2 MXene (CTAB-Sn(IV)@Ti3C2) via a facile liq.-phase cetyltrimethylammonium bromide (CTAB) prepillaring and Sn4+ pillaring method.  The interlayer spacing of Ti3C2 MXene can be controlled according to the size of the intercalated prepillaring agent (cationic surfactant) and can reach 2.708 nm with 177% increase compared with the original spacing of 0.977 nm, which is currently the max. value according to our knowledge.  Because of the pillar effect, the assembled LIC exhibits a superior energy d. of 239.50 Wh kg-1 based on the wt. of CTAB-Sn(IV)@Ti3C2 even under higher power d. of 10.8 kW kg-1.  When CTAB-Sn(IV)@Ti3C2 anode couples with com. AC cathode, LIC reveals higher energy d. and power d. compared with conventional MXene materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr3iZJOAbsOfbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljCZIOWjx9yCg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitFanu7vE&amp;md5=0cc097e0cff81862a50d620d054dae92</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1016/j.jechem.2017.08.004"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.; Zhang, Z.; Zhou, Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MXene-Based Materials for Electrochemical Energy Storage</span>.  <span class="citation_source-journal">J. However, conventional charge storage through ion intercalation or double-layer formation cannot satisfy the requirements of such applications owing to the slow kinetics of ion intercalation and the small capacitance of the double layer.  The present work demonstrates that the pseudocapacitance of the nanosheet compd. MXene Ti2C achieves a higher specific capacity relative to double-layer capacitor electrodes and a higher rate capability relative to ion intercalation electrodes.  By utilizing the pseudocapacitance as a neg. electrode, the prototype Na-ion full cell consisting of an alluaudite Na2Fe2(SO4)3 pos. electrode and an MXene Ti2C neg. electrode operates at a relatively high voltage of 2.4 V and delivers 90 and 40 mAh g-1 at 1.0 and 5.0 A g-1 (based on the wt. of the neg. electrode), resp., which are not attainable by conventional electrochem. energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrGbG1IuL6ZLrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljCZIOWjx9yCg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXotlaitrg%253D&amp;md5=b97a6937c162bb790a4949b87257c217</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1021/acs.jpclett.5b00868"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dall’Agnese, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Taberna, P.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Viscoelastic properties of battery electrodes in contact with electrolyte solns. may affect the electrodes' cycling performance.  However, they are not easily assessed by in situ measurements.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Porous heterostructured MXene/carbon nanotube composite paper with high volumetric capacity for sodium-based energy storage devices</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie, Xiuqiang; Zhao, Meng-Qiang; Anasori, Babak; Maleski, Kathleen; Ren, Chang E.; Li, Jingwen; Byles, Bryan W.; Pomerantseva, Ekaterina; Wang, Guoxiu; Gogotsi, Yury</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The global availability of sodium and a possibility to avoid the use of copper current collectors make electrochem. sodium-ion storage attractive for battery and metal-ion capacitor applications.  However, the use of Na instead of Li ions requires different electrode materials that can accommodate larger Na ions and still provide high charging rate and high volumetric capacity.  Herein we report on the fabrication of porous Ti3C2 MXene/CNT composite paper electrodes for sodium-based energy storage devices.  The heterostructure formation was realized by electrostatic attraction between neg. charged 2D MXene nanosheets and pos. charged 1D CNTs.  This method efficiently prevented restacking of MXene nanosheets and produced a well-defined porous structure, thereby facilitating electrolyte transport and access of ions to the electrode and producing functional MXene-based electrodes for sodium-ion storage.  When applied as freestanding electrodes for sodium-ion storage, the built-to-order Ti3C2 MXene/CNTs porous films showed high volumetric capacity of 421 mA h cm-3 at 20 mA g-1, good rate performances, and excellent cycling stability.  Prototype sodium-ion cells were also assembled using the as-prepd. Ti3C2/CNTs anode and Na0.44MnO2 cathode.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitive Electrodes Produced by Oxidant-Free Polymerization of Pyrrole between the Layers of 2D Titanium Carbide (MXene)</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Boota, Muhammad; Anasori, Babak; Voigt, Cooper; Zhao, Meng-Qiang; Barsoum, Michel W.; Gogotsi, Yury</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In summary, we demonstrate a facile strategy for the in situ polymn. of pyrrole confined between Ti3C2Tx layers. XRD and TEM results confirmed that pyrrole intercalated the Ti3C2Tx layers and that the polymer chains are highly aligned. When tested as supercapacitor electrodes, a PPy/Ti3C2Tx composite yielded volumetric capacitance of approx. 1000 F/cm3 and capacitance retention of 92% after 25,000 cycles.  We attribute this high electrochem. performance and excellent cycle life to its self-assembled layered architecture having aligned PPy confined between the conductive Ti3C2Tx monolayers, which leads to high electronic cond., fast reversible redox reactions,and better ion transport due to short diffusion pathways.  Furthermore, the enhanced capacitance is due to the synergistic effect of increased interlayer spacing between the Ti3C2Tx layers due to intercalation of conductive PPy, and due to surface redox processes of the PPy and MXene.  It is important to exactly det. the polymn. mechanism.                 10.1021/acs.chemmater.6b03933</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D29%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D2731-2738%26journal%3DChem.%2BMater.%26author%3DM.%2BBoota%26author%3DM.%2BPasini%26author%3DF.%2BGaleotti%26author%3DW.%2BPorzio%26author%3DM.%2BQ.%2BZhao%26author%3DJ.%2BHalim%26author%3DY.%2BGogotsi%26title%3DInteraction%2Bof%2BPolar%2Band%2BNonpolar%2BPolyfluorenes%2Bwith%2BLayers%2Bof%2BTwo-Dimensional%2BTitanium%2BCarbide%2B%2528MXene%2529%253A%2BIntercalation%2Band%2BPseudocapacitance%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.chemmater.6b03933&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b12155&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.chemmater.6b03933&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interaction of Polar and Nonpolar Polyfluorenes with Layers of Two-Dimensional Titanium Carbide (MXene): Intercalation and Pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Boota, Muhammad; Pasini, Mariacecilia; Galeotti, Francesco; Porzio, William; Zhao, Meng-Qiang; Halim, Joseph; Gogotsi, Yury</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">29</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2731-2738</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This article provides an insight into interaction of synthetic π-conjugated polymers (polyfluorene derivs., PFD) with layers of two-dimensional (2D) titanium carbide (Ti3C2Tx).  Three derivs. with non-polar, polar and charged nitrogen-contg. functionalities were synthesized via the Suzuki polycondensation reaction.  The org.-inorg. PFD/Ti3C2Tx hybrids were prepd. and characterized using x-ray diffraction, and a range of microscopic and spectroscopic techniques to elucidate the host-guest interaction mechanism.  We show that polar polymers with charged nitrogen-contg. ends have the strongest interaction with the Ti3C2Tx layers, yielding an increase in interlayer spacing and large shifts in spectroscopic peaks.  Furthermore, the effect of polymer backbone juxtaposition between Ti3C2Tx layers on pseudocapacitance is discussed in detail.  Our results suggest that new org. materials capable of intercalation between the layers of Ti3C2Tx and other MXenes may be used in design of hybrid structures for high-performance energy storage applications and beyond.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpU437G_JU_o7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lghzgsEQBbNww"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXjsVCmtbY%253D&amp;md5=11ff3dbfe03e9d02f950d0e07ee9be9c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms2664"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mashtalir, O.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Naguib, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mochalin, V.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intercalation and delamination of layered carbides and carbonitrides</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mashtalir Olha; Naguib Michael; Mochalin Vadym N; Dall'Agnese Yohan; Heon Min; Barsoum Michel W; Gogotsi Yury</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1716</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Intercalation and delamination of two-dimensional solids in many cases is a requisite step for exploiting their unique properties.  Herein we report on the intercalation of two-dimensional Ti3C2, Ti3CN and TiNbC-so called MXenes.  Intercalation of hydrazine, and its co-intercalation with N,N-dimethylformamide, resulted in increases of the c-lattice parameters of surface functionalized f-Ti3C2, from 19.5 to 25.48 and 26.8 ÅA, respectively.  Urea is also intercalated into f-Ti3C2.  Molecular dynamics simulations suggest that a hydrazine monolayer intercalates between f-Ti3C2 layers.  Hydrazine is also intercalated into f-Ti3CN and f-TiNbC.  When dimethyl sulphoxide is intercalated into f-Ti3C2, followed by sonication in water, the f-Ti3C2 is delaminated forming a stable colloidal solution that is in turn filtered to produce MXene 'paper'.  The latter shows excellent Li-ion capacity at extremely high charging rates.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQzZ-BvcJeO7tenUz0lpNqnfW6udTcc2eZI3zcIl3zBd7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3srlvVOnuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=d2353c4d0005aa57aeff161518f98e51</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201500604"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mashtalir, O.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lukatskaya, M. W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gogotsi, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Amine-Assisted Delamination of Nb<sub>2</sub>C MXene for Li-Ion Energy Storage Devices</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amine-Assisted Delamination of Nb2C MXene for Li-Ion Energy Storage Devices</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mashtalir, Olha; Lukatskaya, Maria R.; Zhao, Meng-Qiang; Barsoum, Michel W.; Gogotsi, Yury</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">23</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3501-3506</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MXenes are stacks of 2D early transition metal carbides and carbonitrides of general formula Mn+1XnTx , where M stands for metal atom, X stands for C and/or N, n = 1, 2, or 3, and Tx represents various surface terminations (OH, O, and/or F groups).  Delaminated MXenes can store more charge than their multilayer counterparts; introduction of carbon additives, such as carbon nanotubes (CNTs) into the electrode structure improves ion accessibility to the MXene layers and boosts both specific capacities and resulting rate performances.  So far only Ti3C2Tx has been synthesized and tested in delaminated form.  To delaminate the latter DMSO, DMSO, was used.  In this Communication, our main goal is to report on the delamination of a second representative of the MXene family Nb2CTx using an amine instead of DMSO.  The electrochem. behavior of delaminated Nb2CTx/CNT composite electrodes in Li-ion batteries and supercapacitors are superior to their multilayered counterparts.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGom36pd2doEarVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lghzgsEQBbNww"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXnsFCltrs%253D&amp;md5=ccb60c8d992d93a495989af04a405d86</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201600682"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, S.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered Orthorhombic Nb2O5@Nb4C3Tx and TiO2@Ti3C2Tx Hierarchical Composites for High Performance Li-ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Chuanfang; Kim, Seon Joon; Ghidiu, Michael; Zhao, Meng-Qiang; Barsoum, Michel W.; Nicolosi, Valeria; Gogotsi, Yury</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">23</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4143-4151</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Engineering electrode nanostructures is crit. in developing high-capacity, fast rate-response, and safe Li-ion batteries.  This study demonstrates the synthesis of orthorhombic Nb2O5@Nb4C3Tx (or @Nb2CTx) hierarchical composites via a one-step oxidn. -in flowing CO2 at 850 °C -of 2D Nb4C3Tx (or Nb2CTx) MXene.  The composites possess a layered architecture with orthorhombic Nb2O5 nanoparticles decorated uniformly on the surface of the MXene flakes and interconnected by disordered carbon.  The composites have a capacity of 208 mAh g-1 at a rate of 50 mA g-1 (0.25 C) in 1-3 V vs. Li+/Li, and retain 94% of the specific capacity with 100% Coulombic efficiency after 400 cycles.  The good electrochem. performances could be attributed to three synergistic effects: (1) the high cond. of the interior, unoxidized Nb4C3Tx layers, (2) the fast rate response and high capacity of the external Nb2O5 nanoparticles, and (3) the electron "bridge" effects of the disordered carbon.  This oxidn. method was successfully extended to Ti3C2Tx and Nb2CTx MXenes to prep. corresponding composites with similar hierarchical structures.  Since this is an early report on producing this structure, there is much room to push the boundaries further and achieve better electrochem. performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGre5VYAlHI_7LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lghzgsEQBbNww"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XnsFWls78%253D&amp;md5=f32472aca7b6aa658557ad8f8641d5a5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201607017"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qiu, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Stabilizing the MXenes by Carbon Nanoplating for Developing Hierarchical Nanohybrids with Efficient Lithium Storage and Hydrogen Evolution Capability</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ti3C2 MXene-Derived Sodium/Potassium Titanate Nanoribbons for High-Performance Sodium/Potassium Ion Batteries with Enhanced Capacities</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Yanfeng; Wu, Zhong-Shuai; Zheng, Shuanghao; Wang, Xiaohui; Qin, Jieqiong; Wang, Sen; Shi, Xiaoyu; Bao, Xinhe</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4792-4800</span>CODEN:
